de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls in the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Or grain, or beast, or stone from the mine or similar thing such as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	Or seed, like oats, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Or flowing substance such as water, oil, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When stone or other matter that does not fit nor grow in the ear falls into it, expose the ear to sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, apply a drop of purple oil or oil of cypress, then administer its removal.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make him sneeze with a condy, and plug the nose when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	And lift the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often, pus comes out through this treatment.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come out with pus, apply subtle pincers for its extraction, which are shaped like this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If not, apply an equally subtle small double-edged hook for its extraction.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not come out with the hook, make a flaxen wick and insert its head into the hole of the ear very firmly, and stuff what is around the wick with soft wax so that no air can enter along with the wick.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then treat the wound thoroughly, for often fire is necessary as we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if fire does not come in this way, take glue of which birds are caught, and place some on an instrument that is sharp for the purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and treat with fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it cannot be treated by any of these methods we have said, then quickly cut the ear rather than an abscess, before heat and spasm occur.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	The method of incision is as follows: first, bind the patient's head with a headband, and extract blood according to his condition, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the fat depending on it.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the fissure be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone. Then remove it according to your ability and suck rapidly toward your mouth
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	until the treatment is complete and it has healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	and if there is grain inside and it swells, administer removal.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot be expelled, use the spatula very gently in this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And prepare an incision for that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is soft due to the moisture in the ear until you have made several incisions.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract it with fine forceps and by sucking it out, as we have said before so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing remedies and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it should jump out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, slender and light, and warm them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	And place the patient's ear over a hole, and let them lean out with their feet from the other side, and strike an additional stone upon the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	And do not stop striking stone with stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see this, take a reed and insert one end into the ear, and apply fire to the other end until the better part of the reed is burnt.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then repeat this process with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In extracting the beast, if it has a small body like that of a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the section on divisions.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it has a large body that one can feel, then arrange for the extraction of pin-holes.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lightest thing to remove that there is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms entangled in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section on divisions and treating secretions, and the treatment does not work, then you must examine the ear in the sunlight.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if no worms appear, take some fine pincers and treat them; if none appear, then use the instrument that has their shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And [the ear] is narrow underneath but wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And thrust the most subtle tip into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then thoroughly suck out all the contents.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, stuff the canal with cotton around it as I have said for stones.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not emerge as we have said, apply the distillations that ancient doctors have proven effective in expelling worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, of which this is the form as you see it:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is made of silver or brass, narrow below at small openings, and broad above to pour out (the distillation);
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	to compress within the distillation with an instrument of brass made well for this purpose, and if you wish to use a razor, wrap it around the point, lined with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour in your oil or juice, whatever medicine you wish from among those inside the cane, and let the cane be placed within the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then push in the razor along with all of the cotton, and press your hand gradually until the oil is distilled or reaches the end of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient should feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warm from the fire, unless one is distilling into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And ensure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without an opening in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men due to blockage of a wound or wax inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes pierce through the ear, so it cannot be seen.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and at times the hole appears outside the opening, and you can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Therefore, the one that pierces through and cannot be seen is quickly healed in many cases, and for this, when it can be seen, you must place the patient's ear in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the inflammation evident, operate on this entire area of which it consists:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be sharp and cutting in front and behind, completely smooth so it does not harm the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the inflammation is of newborn flesh or within the ear itself, hold it with fine pincers and cut away lightly, until all this flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is complete in the ear, take a subtle light razor and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel inflammation causing the patient itching when heard, pierce lightly, and be careful not to damage the ear nerves;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then insert in the ear an ointment tent according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this on any day when the wound is healed, take a linen cloth and dampen it with pink water, then powder it with ground vitriol.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you remove the cloth and apply another damp cloth made of wax mixed with rose oil until the swelling is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and employ other treatments that stop the bleeding as described in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the paper's flesh.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These eyelids that become moist on paper and are dry, it is necessary to separate them with tongs and pincers, and cut off a piece of the root with a small spade.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then place on it ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it cannot be peeled away, then perform a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer moves after the incision.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and they often return when something remains in their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned away and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often come into the eyes things that appear like hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "grandine," an assembly of thick moisture within the cornea above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The treatments are as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take note if the "grandine" moves from one side to another, as this is something that should be known easily.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Making a wide incision, then flay each part lightly, taking it with forceps, and cutting it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut without piercing the membrane slightly, it causes no harm to the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the tear is large, you should sew it together with a stitch, healing it until it is sound;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not apply force, for the ointments will restore it quickly, promoting flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	If the clot descends into the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the membrane and stretch out the clot with forceps, cutting it and pressing from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the membrane is separated by incision, it causes no harm.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the cataract is removed, irrigate the eye with salt water, and treat the place where pus arises until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	From the fat of eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that forms on the membranes of children's eyes more than adults', and it greatly harms their eyes, causing them to have cataracts in the morning, and they cannot bear the sunlight due to tears rushing to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this they sleep on their faces, and rest above, with their membranes below their eyebrows moist, which swells and covers the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers, feel the dislocation between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of treatment is such that the patient places their head on your lap.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent-like covering in the shape of a circle according to the size that exceeds each part, then place it on top.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two hands from either side so that the excess is gathered within the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit which is not wider than the wound made when opening the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make an incision in the skin precisely until you reach the excess tissue.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in many cases, discharge emerges from the opening, resembling a fragment of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it entirely with a piece of cloth held between your two fingers at the exit, and turn your hand right and left until it is dispersed.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Be careful not to reach into the opening with your spatula until you strike the eyeball and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the discharge does not appear at the beginning of the opening, gently widen the fissure slightly until it becomes visible.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have described, moistening the cloths with oil and water, place them on the spot, and strain them out of bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for those people who grind willow and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it reaches the warm abscess place, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on the eyelids contrary to nature and are left unchecked, they harm the eyes, causing various ailments such as habitual tears, softening of the eyelids, and discharge, ultimately leading to eye damage.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and treatment is done in four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	by fire cauterization together with other medical procedures according to what was discussed in the chapter on cauterization or by medication depending on the case; it is done either through incision and stitching or through canes as I will explain further.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You should place the patient's head on your lap, then turn their affected eyelid towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is turned inward, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, insert a needle through it with a thread attached;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	And be it near the edge of the paper where the hairs grow beside them, and draw the thread over all the paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then make an incision below the paper beneath the hairs aligned there, cutting all the length with the wide blade from the large hinge to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then extract the thread and place beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper an image of an anchor, like the myrtle leaf, and still it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the paper which is divided everywhere.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	Et if has such who need it cut large quantity of the paper according to how much the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make all the spatula on these two lines that you have marked, and start from the large gash until small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the fissure be near natural hairs in thickness of a root, then insert unicorn's horn into one of two angle of heart, and then scrape away everything;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then join the two lips with one seam of needle and all the fine thread of wool, wipe away blood, and remove excess hair on both eyebrows with any adhesive substance, if you wish to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, then take no care of it, just leave the stitches and threads for three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound without stitches using drying and binding agents, for paper adheres to the healing of the wound and its reunion, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and it is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And cut the paper into a shape that resembles the myrtle leaf, as we have described, to three ounces apart according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut this top part with small equal forces according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the object is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and place it in the middle of the shape.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and pull another thread towards the large armpit, and the second thread towards the small [armpit], and gather between your two fingers the threads evenly.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin onto which you have sewn, as we have told you, then join the two lips of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess appears at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes the hairs of the papule turn white:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But the suturing on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of fractures follows this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And make paper and cut it into this according to what I said, then make two fractures per page, and also two fine threads as long as the width of the paper, which is the size of a spatula.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And cut two heads at either end where you hold the threads.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then carefully attach one to the other on top of the paper's eyelet, and pull the two threads from each part.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	Leave it like this for a few days, and the skin that was constricted will die, blacken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he delays, strike it with force, then treat it until it is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is closed, if the scab has risen, they will no longer prick the hair;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two chains that you will make according to this figure, and with this measure of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The works are such that you take a fine needle, and insert into it a thread of soft and delicate silk;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then join the heads and tie each one finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then pass through the shaft another fine silk thread quickly, and tie the ends of the thread together.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the patient's head on your lap;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is delicate and precise work, then insert the needle into the base of the hair follicle, pierce through the skin until you draw it out above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair up to its base, and insert that hair back into the follicle, whether there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out along with the natural hair follicle.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the follicle is damaged and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull on the hair below to extract the entire follicle through the opening above so that you can see it with your eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Thus, you will draw out the dart and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hair withers in its place and flesh grows back over it.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair with those of natural growth, and let it be raised along with them until they grow longer and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or scrofula comes to the eye, there are two ways it may arise.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One is natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly due to wounds or incisions, from cauterization, and similar procedures.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	The way of working on it is that you split the abscess and separate its lips, putting in linen pads, binding them until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And you must not use anything that dries or tightens in their treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do so, the illness will return worse than before.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening agents such as fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and rose water or another [liquid] and flax seeds are boiled, and diaqilun ointments melted in any oil, and a poultice is prepared, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the secret of your treatment is that you must be careful not to restore it exactly as it was before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these treatments we have mentioned are only temporary solutions to this illness so that it does not return as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is inflammation, truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidents come from wounds, tears, cauterization, and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the method of work is as follows: take a needle with double thread and insert it into the flesh, piercing from left armpit to right, so that the thread emerges at two points in the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then stretch the flesh above completely over the needle, and cut it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape on the paper returns as it should be, that is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take a razor and place it in the gap, turn the paper over, and make two incisions on either side inside the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the two sides of the two incisions in the corners that you have cut be joined together, forming an angle so that when they are assembled, it resembles the shape of the Greek letter I.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the amount its edges extend below, from what follows under the paper, then join together the two separated parts and sew them up with a woolen thread.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with the softening medications we mentioned before, and apply dressings until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the wound resulted from a tear or suture or cauterization, you should make an incision directly below the hairline of the skin, according to what was mentioned earlier.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then sever between the two lips of a wound, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the procedure according to the form of the illness, as it is very diverse in form, and wise surgeons use all their power and skill to restore the body's shape to its natural state;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patients themselves, according to what is required for treatment and tools in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the papery skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this fusion occurs in the hands of men such that the film over the eye is stuck with the white part, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, you must therefore insert the tip of a razor underneath the film and lift it upwards.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And stretch them with pincers until you cut off that which is open to the subtle spatule, but make sure it's not too sharp nor too cutting so that the patient does not suffer from a spatula that's too sharp causing harm to the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And make your incision such that you peel off the gathered assembly lightly so that the paper returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And it is purified all that assembly, sometimes with salt water in the eye, and others with clean water, and collarbone.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place between the paper and eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye moist wool mixed with egg white.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after three days, make use of the collarbone and hot compresses until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the eyelash's nail
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: 
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	She is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another that is not nervous, but appears like white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and thought to be hardened by pincers, cannot be done so.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both appearances begin towards the large corner of the eye, and grow bit by bit until it covers all vision, all light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And for the manner of incision, the patient should put their head in a sound position, then open their eyes wide;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	And take the paper with your hand, then curl your nail around the small pincers, and extend it above [the eye].
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	Then take a needle, and insert a horse hair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	Double the point of the needle slightly and insert it between the nail and flesh, then pierce through with the entire needle, tie the nail to a thread and pull it upward, remove all hair from the side of the nail that covers the affected area and strip its root along with the skin up to the cuticle; finally use a sharp knife and small forceps to cut away any remaining tissue at the base of the wound and leave the natural flesh around the armpit so as not to disturb the usual flow of lymphatic fluid.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes stretch the nail with only onion juice and thread, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then scrape off all of the soft skin, which is how it appears:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And ensure that the soft skin does not touch or tear the fleshy membrane, and that the plumule is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	After the incision, put a pinch of ground silt into the eye, and apply some lead oxide ointment, leaving it on until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the probe cannot enter it, this similar appearance of a nail has often been treated by doctors.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the section above, and if you see them cut, then work on the eye of the patient, and take a light spatule with a sharp point according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And lift the eyelid carefully, and if you see that it does not lessen and the reason presses, then distil from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red copper, both crushed, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then begin the other work according to this same procedure until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of flesh in the eyelid damages the eye severely, then suspend it with an ointment, and cut off a part but not all, so that no liquid comes from tears.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill red eye drops made of litharge into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some men's eyes are sometimes born red, covering the pupil and spreading over the corneas, turning outwards, and looking like a rose of balsam.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the work is that the patient puts their head into your lap, then you open their eyes and roll all that red flesh onto hooks suitable for it, holding it firmly in place.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut off the first flesh with a scalpel, and continue cutting all of it with a razor until you reach the end, taking care not to harm the eye during your work.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And the incision should be like that of a spatoulum, as we have said in the chapter about nail incisions and small forceps which remove it, as its form after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all flesh is removed, fill it with melted beeswax or drip red copper sulphate on it and similar corrosive medicines, then cover the eye with cotton wool dipped in egg white so that abscess heat may be sure to leave.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	if anything remains there, and hot blood overflows you, and abscess heat is doubted, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing medicines for hot abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do likewise whenever flesh has been adjusted in the eye by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak eye in its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	And regarding accidental wounds, in metalworking;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Do not insert your hand into any of these procedures until you see that the limb is suitable for this treatment.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These red veins that are visible under the eye hinder vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary that you first examine the eye to see if it is sound or diseased and whether there are other ailments aside from this.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Therefore, proceed in the following manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap and then apply pressure to the veins accordingly based on your understanding; ensure that those applying the pressure are also skilled, with this treatment being done twice as frequently.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they are two inches apart by degrees inside the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then bind those veins firmly but carefully, wiping away any blood that emerges after a short time until you see the veins receding from the eye.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And be sure to protect the eye from being wounded by the points of spatulas, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your task such that you cut only those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red gallnuts to corrupt that which remains of the cataract.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	If you are unable to collect all of these at that hour, make a plaster over the eye with things soothing for the pain, and leave it there for some days until the pain is soothed and the hot abscess assured, then recommence according to this manner which is before until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	And that is the form of cauterization:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The surgeon calls "arissati" a fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with cautery and medicine for a burning abscess as I have previously mentioned, and it is not healed, if there is pus inside that you must cut open over the abscess, there where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is present until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove all the instrument that formed it.
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	It is called an "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron to the form of a head, and be pointed like a file as it appears in its present form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on top of the location of the rotten bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the rot is gone.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Do this several times, then restore the location with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the location is welded together and nothing grows from it, if there is no damage to the body or the bowels, and they remain as such for forty days without renewal or further abscesses, and no bad accident occurs, know that it has healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, then there is another procedure to reconnect the fistula with the nail hole according to this method:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And it is that you uncover the bone for the second time with an iron tool and sharp medicines. When it has been uncovered, take a drill of this form which should be three-sided at the top with a tapering handle like so: [insert image here]
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then place it on the bone near the armpit, and withdraw your hand from the eye by one inch. Then turn the drill around until it pierces through the bone. The patient will feel this as air passes into their fist if they hold their hand over their knuckles.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	And then restore the place with dry medicine, as I have taught you. And when the flesh grows and hardens around the location, it goes down to the knuckles.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	This is a lighter procedure for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the eye socket.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the wound is open all around and there is no interference with the nerve or any narrowing, then you must bind the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then clean it, then place cups or a ventouse without hurting to suck out the air. Then apply to the eye an ointment made of aconite and aloe and incense and gum tragacanth, then strap on the eye, then plaster over with linen bandages.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the method of the bandages is such that you take soft enough bandages and fold each into fourths, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain it from above with a hard bandage, and resume the cups to suck without hurting;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cups and keep the eye strained day and night, and if the binding loosens, you must strain it strongly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the binding after day and night, and if you see the eye improving, it is good.
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it begins to peel, replace the poultice and cloths and the binding, as well as the cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From rupture of dry skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption occurs in the dark membrane, it then appears and escapes from the sheets like grains of resin, and it is terrible to behold.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it severed, the treatment is such that you insert a needle into the root of one part below until you reach the other above, then thread another needle with a doubled length of string from the other side.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	And pierce it, leaving the first needle in place as per its arrangement.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	Then cut the doubled string and bind one part of the membrane around it tightly, then remove the needle and place a moist linen cloth soaked in egg white over the eye.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	And leave it until the hair grows back with the eyelid, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is bound with cloth in a circle on each side until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	If the eye shows great inflammation, pierce it with a fine spatula that reaches right through the eye, and drain the white moisture and lower the eyelid, then enter immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease, called "alcunnati", is only a tumor that forms in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the way of appearance for the procedure is that you should have the patient sit on an equipped and straight chair, then take their head between both hands and move it until you see the bow coming above your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, do not go down and uncover the light, and let the patient see things as they should.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the bow is not equipped as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	have the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make a hole in the corneal tissue through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the cornea, until the bow appears.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is out, drip into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fennel and honey, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Water from the eyes.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have examined the similarities of waters in the process of division, and what is required to puncture [them].
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	so operate according to healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and tie their healthy eye shut very firmly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper of your eye to their left hand if the eyes are on the left side, or to their right hand if the eyes are on the right side.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called "almagda", or with your left hand, if the eyes are right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the tip of the instrument near the crown by a mark as thin as a hair in that white part of the eye towards the lower eyelid, then push the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that "almagda" reaches the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the measure of "almagda's" path is exactly the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the dark part.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	you will see the bone in this paper due to the clarity of the corneal tissue, and you can place the instrument up until where water is present, then express it below a voice after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water drains now, the patient sees before them and an instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	after replace it small and if the water rises again through another passageway place force with the instrument when it is fully inserted and does not rise then remove the balm slowly while turning your hand back and forth.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then replace some water with a little bit of celandine and leave this in the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply oil-soaked gauze or wet linen to the eye from outside, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin with plenty of egg on it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the ointment cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument known as 'alberit', of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	and therefore perforate the conjunctiva only, do not go too deep but make it a subtle place, then insert the balm as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And when finishing the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed where they can lie on their back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	Remain still, avoiding all movement, eat light foods, and do not move their head to the right or left. They should be bound according to their condition until three days have passed.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then untie them in the same dark room and test their vision. Show them some objects, then retie them again until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And you must not do this during the treatment or after an incision just now, but rather take care of it, as fluid may rapidly rise.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess becomes hot, you must remove the eye before the seventh day, and treat it as you would for an abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is calmed, uncover the eye and place a small piece of gold on its face to cover for one day, and remain in that dark room thereafter.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then take them out of the house little by little, and if they relapse into their condition...
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciple should interfere in such cases.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from Iran, who told us that in his country they make pierced amulets, from which water is extracted, but I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, for those who do not know them see them.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let it be made of pure brass;
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of the ears be made from this same subtle material, while the back end is in three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there arise from eggs different chariots joined together, some of which look like many-footed scorpions;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And if there be such that the chariot is ornamented with variegated hues, while its body is soft of good colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	Therefore in those chariots which are soft but not ornamented, it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands towards the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and work his nostrils, and apply the ointment to those parts, and treat them forcefully.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then grasp what you may sustain with a thin, sharp spatula from one side, until you know that the tissue is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, open it entirely with the thin instruments gently, so that nothing is left behind.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it overpowers you, cauterize the abscess as required;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood flow ceases and all tissues are removed, then apply cold vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If it doesn't work, and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healed.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if the moisture doesn't pierce as it should, know that there is cartilage in the bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you must insert a piece of linen thread slightly thicker, knotted at both ends by our hands, and with one or two fingers' width space between them.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	Have the patient take hold of the thread's head in his fist with all his strength and pull it while sniffing until it comes out through the nostril into the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	Children often do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to try it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and squeeze one after the other carefully, being mindful of the cord they are attached to.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this so that you know the night has corrupted that flesh, then draw out the cord, wipe away the blood, and wet the cord with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has eroded all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Then place in the nose a plug of lime for several days until it is healed, and if they need any drying medicines, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the shape of the instrument to purge the head, for which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	and it is made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, just like a tube, and it leads there too.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish to see it, make an enclosed tube for yourself, and let the instrument be full so as to purge the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and hold it to the head with your hand when you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often there arises in the head of the nose an illness which is called 'telul', and it grows to become large over time, such that it becomes a visible thing.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all flesh, then place a hot iron or burning medicine on it.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay cutting it until it becomes large, take note if it is hard, with a dark hue, and poor scent.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron, for this is an abscess advanced, as when one cuts into it a great illness arises in the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in hue, and you see that it can be entirely cut away, then evacuate the patient and proceed with cutting without fear, treating the wound with drying and astringent substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn [back] up.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the cartilage-related work of this chapter continues for a long time, it provides little benefit, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then when this happens to someone, one must consider if the wound is fresh and contains all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then sew the two lips together with a stitch, then treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the lips are already torn apart on both sides, you must scrape away all the flesh of their hearts until they bleed, then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and hold them in place, and apply powder of dragon's blood and ground incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Put the powders on top with a strong poultice or another sealing plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way of stitching is such that you bring together the ends:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in regards to sewing up the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	From the lips of apostems.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Men's hands within the lips develop hard abscesses, similar to corns, small and large;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then it is necessary to turn back the lips, split open each abscess, take pincers and break them apart in every part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then wash the area after the incision with powdered glass until the blood is stemmed;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it exposed, treating the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	On the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there arises on the gums flesh grown close [to them], which the ancients call 'albulus'
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	Thus you must hold it with tongs, cut it at its root, and let out the pus or blood;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then place on it ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	And if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	It will not return after the cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of wounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes shells gather at the root of teeth inside the mouth between gums: hard, ugly things.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are black and yellow and green, as decay reaches the gum, and their teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	you must make the patient sit between your hands, and their shoulder should be in yours, and pull out teeth or tartar that appears until nothing remains there;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and do the same with blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other discolorations, until they are cleansed.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at the first cause, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, repeat on the second day and the third until you have removed all of it.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that the teeth require different shapes of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the work requires, because the rasp used to clean outside the teeth has a different shape than those used between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	When treating tooth pain, it is necessary to delay the extraction as long as you can, for this should not be done lightly.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very tall structure, until such time as there is no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to extract, you must be certain of the tooth causing pain.
