Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	The pain often troubles the patient, who believes it is in a healthy tooth, leading to the extraction of good teeth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not subside because of this, as long as the evil is present, for we have already witnessed it in these soldiers.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the offending tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth thoroughly. Use a sharp spatula to protect the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then loosen it with your fingers or with delicate pliers at the first notch and extract it until it is well dislodged, then firmly close the pliers;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and have the patient's shoulder in your lap between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if there is no fracture, take one of these instruments and gently insert it into each side, moving it like you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and worn down, it is necessary to fill it with linen where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it delicately with forceps, so it does not break when extracted;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and much bleeding work is required around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care not to break it during extraction, leaving any part behind, as this can cause the patient greater pain due to the root's cunning nature.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeon, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the cartilage and fail to manage what we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause great harm through their ignorance due to the roots that remain or the cartilage they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is extracted, clean the place with wine or oil and silk thread.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if there is bleeding, which often happens, then fill the place with crushed green vitriol.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	if that doesn't work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, with which one moves teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you are extracting the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling (the tooth), and they should be well-made iron, and toothed in order to hold it firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary to place wet cotton soaked in butter on top for one or two days until the area softens, then you can insert the forceps known as "algefri", which resemble a stork's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and are made inside like a file, which is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge from all these tongs, you must uncover the flesh all around the root and insert the instrument known as "althali", which is a plainch, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	and it should be thick and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, use all the instruments, which come after forming these shapes:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one requires assistance from this tool with two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are placed in front of the teeth, and from this tool resembling large tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	and let this instrument be strong so that it does not break, and know that there are many dental instruments;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not listed here;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and wise masters find their own instruments themselves, according to the work they do and the illness presented, for there are such varied ailments that ancient teachers did not instruct on an instrument for each one; if a bone of the carriage or other bones is broken, seek out the appropriate instruments I have told you about, and use gestures, which are formed like this:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And they [the hairs] are thick and well-adhering to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is bone rot, and it is small, so remove all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and they are ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth is newly born and not in its rightful place, and it cannot be treated or filed:
adonques lou raie;	then extract it.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if there is air with the tooth, take this instrument which has this form, and it resembles a small beak, being sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hit it repeatedly with a hammer many times to harden the tooth, and to avoid moving others, and if it is visible enough that you can file it, then use this kind of lime as shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like a file from which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and with the file one sharpens the teeth little by little, gently, so that they do not move as it cuts;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the whole flat surface at each edge is ground to a fine point by any sharpener, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, it must be filed until smooth so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth wanes
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth loosen, either due to impact or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without their teeth coming loose, and you have treated them with constricting medicine, but it is not effective;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	If they must be restrained, use a golden wire, for silver wire turns green and corrodes, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the wire be neither too small nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you wish to guide the teeth back into place, take the wire and loop it double between two healthy teeth, then pass the ends through the gaps left by the missing teeth, until you come out near a sound tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then repeat the procedure until you reach the starting point, then carefully and gently withdraw your hand until it is free.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And ensure the wire is secured at its base, so that it cannot slip off the root of the tooth.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the shoulder bone with a saw using pincers, and put it back together, placing it between two healthy teeth, so that it does not injure the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave it like this as tight as possible so that it remains in place; and if it loosens or the threads become twisted, tighten it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains like this for a long time and serves its purpose, this is the shape of teeth and how to align two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, it should be replaced in its place, fresh for fresh, as we have said before.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And make sure only the wise and experienced are involved, sometimes a tooth made of cow bone is used to replace the missing one; it is placed where needed, secured as described earlier, and serves for many years.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut loose the tongue's bond
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this ligament comes from underneath the tongue or is natural, depending on one's birth.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or due to an injury of a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth, placing their head in your hand and lifting their tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve of the tongue, until it is separated from its sheath, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is due to an immediate injury, then he must pull out the thorn and cut widely on that ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and ensure that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which lies underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift up the place with rosewater and oil, or cold water, then put a linen swab beneath the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient be bathed each night to prevent the place from becoming putrid.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is discharge of blood, then apply powdered vitriol to the place;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood returns, then cauterize with the small circular cautery, which is good for this purpose;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it become discoloured or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining towards inflammation, and there is moisture present, then apply the unguent, and make an incision with a fine spatula, and release it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood threatens to overwhelm your work, then apply crushed vitriol until it is extinguished, and return to your work until everything is treated.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a plaster of flax and silk, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	At times, there are growths that form in the throat called "godaths," properly known as the two tonsils; when you treat them, as we have said before, and they do not heal, then take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If this is a hard abscess of little sense and false colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron, also because of the loss of blood.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it until it is ripe, and then you shall open it, or else it would burst by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of white colour around and the root is subtle, prepare your instruments to cut, but first make sure that the abscess calms down and is relieved.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then let the patient sit before the sun, and their head be in your hand, and open their mouth and grasp the tongue between your hands, and press it down under all the instrument, from which this is formed.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and whether of silver or fine brass like a knife
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue with all these instruments, and see the abscess, take the lancet and insert it into the almond, then draw it out as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and draw out any material with it from the wound, then cover the instrument with cotton, of which this is the shape, resembling forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and however the head is curved, and one side to another, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, shape it using the pliers, which also has a similar form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have treated one of the almonds, treat the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and vinegar, and if there is still bleeding, then gargle the patient with water or boiled pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things until the bleeding stops.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so treat them just like the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed inside her throat, specifically a small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained like this for even one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess had risen to such an extent that two tubes were inserted through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore made haste to insert a thin rod, and passed it through one nostril, then drew out a large portion of bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then refit it elsewhere through the other nostril, and the surgeon opened his mouth and pressed on his tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After inserting the lancet into their abscesses, and cutting a part of it, only a little bit of blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	Thus were the pipes of her throat unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and she did not stop having this abscess cut over a long period.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess regrew again, filling up the space I had emptied so it became very large once more.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I tricked her, and cauterized the inside of her throat.
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus it remains without growth;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And separate from these parts, and be only as God made them after me.
de l’uve	Of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the kingdom descends to the egg, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is excessively thick and round, it is called an "egg".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the wound has healed but remains delicate, then you must cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and one which is rounded, gathered together, and not elongated;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if it is bloody or false colored or black, you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the lancet into the eye, draw it downwards, and cut at an angle of 45 degrees with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising both testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut beyond the natural limit, only removing the excess.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you cut more, it will harm their voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have mentioned for the incision of two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you should employ an engine for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is quick, sharp pain.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient place their head in your lap, and then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, moisten it with hot water that is neither too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the tip of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have a lock of hair on the head where one applies the medicine, like the bristles of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine onto the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, without it reaching the throat or hurting them;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it onto the eye, for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it blacken and the stinging from the medicine subsides;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, then dampen the cotton with the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton into the eye until the cotton rests on the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and fall out after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the medicine cautery, do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And immerse them in cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take galangal and hyssop and oregano and chamomile and mugwort and similar herbs, combine all or any of them in a pot, add vinegar, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pot should be well-sealed with thick clay, and inside the pot place an instrument that has been hollowed out in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	It should be made of silver or copper, and one end of it is inserted into the patient's mouth so that the vapour rises to the eye through the tear duct until the eye is cured.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After you start again often, until the wound dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's appearance when it is hot, because many things happen there.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not treat this like an abscess which is declining in heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and put a piece of egg inside the patient's mouth so that their mouth does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Because the egg piece will prevent the steam from burning the mouth, and this is a good treatment with an overall benefit.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often it happens that there is bone or fish spine stuck in the throat, or any other foreign object.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Thus, you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the palate with all your might so that you can observe movement.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And for that which does not reveal itself and remains in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps thus the thing will be expelled by vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navew, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And tie to the sponge a thread, then swallow it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	When it arrives at its place, it will be expelled, and then you must pull on the thread.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take a lead instrument of this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have its head raised upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest choking occur, nor push against the bone within;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes in the instrument, for he knows where the obstruction lies;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if it goes down, or he pulls out the entire instrument evenly, until it is fully withdrawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	From within the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes surgery is necessary, as I have said in the classification, through medicinal treatment;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, and press their tongue with the instrument I mentioned to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a small hook, or use delicate forceps that are fit for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not effective, take a hairy caterpillar and thrust it into the patient's throat; then insert at the end of the caterpillar a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient drink cold water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open their mouth, pour it in as if they were swallowing, and move their hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood meets the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall as we said, then smoke the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the eye fumigation.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall without fail.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, through which hole the head of the instrument should be placed.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then I pour my fumigation into it, and the patient places the head of the cane in their mouth, closing their mouth so that no smoke escapes but instead goes up to the sinuses.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the sinuses will run, if they do not discharge then repeat the fumigation several times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And let the patient suffer from thirst, eating salty or sour things but drinking no water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Then they will need to be expelled by this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument used to remove leeches, when it can be seen, resembles bent pliers for inserting them into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a bird, and has the roughness of a file, such that whatever it grasps, it cannot release.
et vez ci la forme:	and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many types of abscesses, as described by different sources in this book, and they vary in their puncturing and cutting.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways that differ in appearance and what they hold.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for those on parts of the body where they are moist.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses on soft parts differ from those which occur in joints, each having its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And for abscesses, one should not puncture them when the bowels are dead according to their fullness.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for those of such that need piercing when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, just like abscesses which appear near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses appear near joints, and it is left until it has rotted all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where an abscess is near the main member, and if you delay piercing until it is dead, it will harm the main member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Where it is near the foundation, pierce it before it dies.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And one must not pierce a ripe abscess without completing the digestion process, except for the one near the foundation, which will rot completely and become elongated from within, resulting in a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the work of perforating an abscess which is ready according to its development, and this happens when the pain subsides, and there is a reduction in feverish symptoms, and the lessening of pain and redness, and from swelling and sharpening at the head of the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must make the perforation sit above where the abscess is more dependent, and where it appears to move;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be made along the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or at joints, nerves, and arteries, and all places equally where there is no bend.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those which bend, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in soft tissue, it's best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed to be digested completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before that, the poison from it would spread throughout the body, and it is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And perhaps they harden the lips and its depths.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to someone an abscess is pierced according to the width of its body, according to this which the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	Then you must treat small abscesses, small openings.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	And in large abscesses, large openings, and many cracks according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if you encounter such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the heart, to remove it.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become like rags, and is dead, then you must proceed as with boils.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And if you encounter such cases that are split into three angles, and there are some from which one must also remove like the leaves of myrtle, just as with abscesses in the groin.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such people where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head [referring to those with abscesses that do not yet have a visible 'head' or core], just like soft superficial abscesses, you must pierce them fully.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large, and it has formed a great swelling, and you pierce it, do not extract all of the pus at once, but only part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop up the abscess until the next day, then extract any remaining pus promptly.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this multiple times gradually until all of the swelling has subsided.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman with child, or small children, or elderly and infirm men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the spirits twitch with the exit of the bile, which may cause the patient's death, and you would not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Be very careful with this chapter, and once you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound dry, and look to see if the abscess wound is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it's an open gash, then apply lint bandages or old cotton rags.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it's a large abscess with many perforations, you must insert a bandage into each one so that they lie next to each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut away a piece of the skin over the abscess and stretched it back, then you must fill it with old cotton or shredded linen cloth without moisture, binding it tight until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove it, and treat until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if hemorrhages occur in your work, bring cold and light water, and wet some cloths, and place them on the bleeding site multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the flow of blood persists, provide management and treatment, along with the powders I've mentioned in this book, especially during winter when the skin or abscess is very sensitive. In such cases, it's necessary to apply moistened tents and linen cloths soaked in warm wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it's during summer when the skin is fleshy, use moistened linen cloths soaked in water and oil or cold wine and oil, leaving them on for up to three days as we've mentioned.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then open the abscess, dry it, and treat it as necessary until it's healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be universally known regarding abscess treatment:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	For I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	scurvy
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the brain of the head comes out small abscesses, and are made like nets, just like the breast of a hen, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such where there is also moisture like blisters;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if there are such cases that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt as the artery does not behave contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of incision is such that you must try every instrument which is called an "introducer", from where its shape comes afterwards, and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if there is moisture, they will push it from above with forceps.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, it leaves the skin that contained said moisture bare and raw, for it returns when nothing is left there.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, use water and salt, apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And these will heal what has remained from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And you may reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you know for certain that nothing remains from the night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with an ointment that is suitable, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds in fat tissue, cut into it along this length.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And throw out your thumbs, and peel it from all sides, and apply all of your treatment to draw out the pus where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery goes against you, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also of the abscess if it is hard, and of cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the hard abscess and the moist one is lighter, for they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	and if in any of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, like in this case of an abscess I cut open on an elderly woman's head;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had cut it with an iron, they would have made as much of a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come on the head, especially those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of their ears, the opening should always be made as close to their base as possible, so as to remove the pus;
et les cure si com il covient.	And treat them as required.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the arms, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere on the body, and they are very common, and grow intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	Each scrofula is properly within its area, just like the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And there are many similar cases to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In the one that you see with good positioning to touch, and it resembles the body's color, and moves in every direction without being attached to the neck veins or artery nor the channel, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	You must cut it from above and peel off the skin on every side, then spread apart the two lips of the wound with tweezers if you need to, just as we have said for abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and strike it here and there, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula not be sharp or cutting, lest your hand slip, and don't go too far ahead so as to avoid cutting what you shouldn't.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery and it won't let you work on it, then apply ground glass to the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and bind up the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	leave it be until the abscess is healed, and the wound softens, and begins to putrefy.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then look for any small scrofula on your index finger; if there are any, cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large wound at the root of the scrofula, you must not cut into that root, but rather bind it tightly with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off on its own without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, since there is no excess left due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut the root of it, and drain [it], and stitch [it] as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Scrofula that has suppuration should be pierced where it appears to die.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it as mentioned before, depending on the case, then apply cautery with ointment and similar things to that which remains of the suppuration.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleansed, apply healing ointment to promote flesh regeneration until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke of the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I have never seen it done in our land, only written about in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with difficulty breathing, it is necessary to remove the obstruction in the throat known as the epiglottis;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And if no aid is provided through this method, it is because all the veins and passages of the patient are affected by abscesses that are hot in the mouth, throat or both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the passage of breathing, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid suffocation and death.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we divide it beneath three circles or four in a small transverse slit between two of them, rather than by the quantity of the cut on the surface, not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that has no flesh and where vessels run lengthwise.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are afraid, they must stretch out the skin of the throat to all sides and cut down into the heart until it reaches the windpipe.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And remove the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut into the surface as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the interruption of the flow through the cane which must pass through the broken area and through the defect of the way.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for one period.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed by which strangulation is doubted, gather together the two lips of the wound from its center, and cut through it completely without the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicine that promotes tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breath defect.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	therefore cover the epiglottis for one who cannot breathe, and they will instead inhale through the wound, thus saving them from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason, the ancients ordered that one leave the wound open until the harmful effect of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they order to suture the wound and treat it until it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called upon to cure her, but found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, knowing that she had not opened a vein nor ruptured her windpipe such that air escaped through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And all the damsel had was that she lost her voice, but later returned to herself;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Because of this, I say that one should not fear an incision to the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	Of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the colour of jaundice, and it occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	et it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one resembles us in flesh, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not appropriate to operate with fire unless it is small, and this has been proven by all the sources.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as our flesh and it does not reach any vein, then cut it like we cut the nails, and treat all its hair if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And stitch it up quickly, and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Des nous
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways for us, of which I will describe all the similarities.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I explain all the differences between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that them is sick with heat and fever until the boiling passes, and the rotting is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat abate.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With us there is no heat, fever or pain, and it contains a cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the colour of the body, and begins like a yolk, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two similarities, either coarse or moist, and very much of colour as I have said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the bone disease 'nout', that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments known as "entromissoires," according to how their form will be used in this chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	and the method of examining abscesses is that you take hold of the moistest part you find in the abscess and turn your fingers back and forth until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the instrument, and take care what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	if running moisture is evident, whatever its colour may be, treat it as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if no moisture issues from the instrument, know that it is greasy and treat it thus by making a cross-shaped incision into it, then seize it with pincers and gently scrape away its skin on either side while you draw out its core along with any threads attached to it.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out whole, then extract it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything is left behind, the wound will reopen multiple times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if even a little is left, and blood grieves you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powder, restrain the wound, and apply warm poultices to draw out the abscess, healing it with other treatments until it is fully healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with something that encourages flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the beating vein opposes you or something else, then hurry and apply crushed vitriol to the place, leaving it there for two or three days until the wound rots, suppressing the boiling of blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to cut what has remained from the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Look here at the shapes of the introducing instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	Large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are three kinds of squares, which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they come in three types:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are like the needles with which we sew sores, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they have been proven to be effective against dark blue fistula abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	And they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of hernia are very similar, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	And if there be hernias with two curves of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	And if there be hernias with three curves, and they too are of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	And if there be hernias with two curves, and also some with one curve only, and they too are of three kinds.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	et all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these to which one applies are sharp, and there are some that only cut in one direction, from which we remove the nerves so as not to damage the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these intrumentals are the handles answered in many, so that the patient does not perceive it at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they should not be used other than in fleshy places like legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to bark peels, according to this form, with which one stops the bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is sometimes placed in a position that heals by closing veins and arteries, and other times according to this grand design:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they appear like female breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must be careful according to this form from line b. until g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing meat, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs low, and is softened due to its size like in women, then cut it into two parts above, through two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one is attached to the other at the end of each one, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b. up to the line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin between the two lips and remove the fat. Apply what we have discussed regarding stitches and powders and any other necessary treatments until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed or the incision is not fully complete due to either the patient's unwillingness to rest or blood loss, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Leave it until the remaining matter and fat is discharged, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are like hard scrofula with sides, and there is moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, treat it as we have said for incising scrofulas, and if the wound becomes hollow, apply cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is closed together, abscesses often result, just as there can be swelling in the vein with an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you recognize it as such for the artery, the abscesses are long in depth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, you sense tightness.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and if it is in the vein, there will be raised lumps on top.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it lies beneath the shoulders and the jaws or in a lot of other places and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	One must therefore avoid the treatment of iron, and one at head should also avoid it, especially in those who are swollen due to an artery rupture above their skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then make an incision at the waist with a circular motion, and carefully separate the artery from its surroundings until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle beneath it, piercing through to the other side, and secure the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you when extracting the two arteries at the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the area between the two ligatures with a probe until the blood which is there has drained out, and the abscess will be opened.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then bring forward the treatment that causes swelling, until the ligature falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with ointment, continuing to do so until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, you must hold with your hand what you can of the abscess along the skin, then insert the needle underneath where you are holding it with your hand, and make it pierce through, having a double thread so that you draw it out from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess as I have told you, with one of two threads from one side to another across both shoulders;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then insert another needle with all of the thread underneath the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and secure the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess so that its excess comes out, then cut the heart's excess and leave what is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on top a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then provide treatments with tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to nerves when they are injured or by too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hands, and in all their joints, whether it is a serious abscess or a minor one, and its colour resembles that of the body, and there is pain in many positions;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	When it is held very tightly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in a perfect part of the body but below the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it moves well from all sides, neither forward nor backward, nor below nor above, and one which is in the joints should not be cut with a knife;
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	Perhaps there would be contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and if it is on the head or forehead, make an incision with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with the hook and peel it, then remove it and sew up the wound, treating it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	It sometimes appears on bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to mushrooms, with delicate roots and a large head;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are small and very large ones among them;
