et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these sides all together, bring the needle back to the starting point at the other side in the way one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And place a space between each stitch equal to the thickness of one thumb.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	These stitches are for a man, and I stitched up a wound on a horse's belly which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was over a palm in size, and the intestines were protruding two palms in length, and the wound was located in the middle of its belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days; I treated him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the surgeon had judged that it would kill him, but this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I did not treat it with any ointment because I was in a place where none could be found nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you of the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and push it from the outer part until it reaches inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced through the heart from right to left, leave the tip of the needle where it is or rests inside after you have pushed it in, and make another hole on the other side from the inner part until it reaches outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this suturing is that you sew it just as furriers do with furs, leaving one side of the needle unthreaded and taking it up again on the other, until the whole suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, as Galen calls it properly, is when anyone does it by joining the two parts together naturally and applying one tip of the needle to the other in such a way that...
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle at the base of the nose, and pierce that spot only, and leave the two nostrils alone.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and pierce it from outside to inside, towards the two nostrils.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Pierce each one from outside to inside, in two other places of the nose that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the binding way, or suturing method, most commonly used.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien says this word, and they testify that one must suture the abdomen with two needles, each having its own thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one needle must be pushed from one side, and another from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, its stitching is more serious than those of other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments about this wound are such as the judgments for other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, rather than moved by the physician, then reset the intestine and sew it.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then apply the powder of burnt animal fat, and if the physician has moved it, then put some fresh ointment so that the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And bind the wound with thread, joining together the lip and the cheek.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound like any other until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you don't have any medicine, apply old cotton wool to it as soon as it starts to produce pus, and move it twice daily until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you suspect that the wound may cause a spread to vital body parts, then it is necessary to wet a light linen cloth with tepid warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the groin and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or inflammation in his bowels, which often happens, then cleanse them with a tepid black wine enema, especially if the inflammation reaches the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from within, knowing that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to treat than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the fragility of its veins, and because of the delicacy of the entire body, and the closeness of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound gapes open, push it back like with the intestine, while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and turned black or green, you must tie the black part so that no blood runs out of it, for there are veins and arteries within;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two heads from below the wound up to outside in order to ease its extraction when the guts fall out, and the wound heals;
de la routure dou boueil	On the rupture of the mouth
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are round and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I saw that a man was wounded in his belly by a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which came discharges and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could, and did not cease to remove the pus until he was healed, and the wound closed up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healed, I feared that the patient had an ailment in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no ill, but he remained in good health, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied up like this:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take large plasters, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the plaster has opened its mouth, put it on both lips, so that it tightens its mouth above them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then cut the plaster's head and this will hold so that it cannot be undone, then put another plaster after in the same way as before, until the wound is fully bound up;
et cout la plaie.	and cut out the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	These chiefs are applied to the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this gut string and make it very smooth, then tie to one end of the gut a fine flax thread twisted around it. Then insert the thread into the needle and pierce through the gut, then pull back up through the rupture.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this method of joining is not false, but according to the way of trust and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it's in one of the major intestines, there will be no remedy nor health without great skill.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is covered and curved.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	Fistula is truly a faulty hardened white knot, where there is no pain felt and it also resembles the quill of a feather.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes it leaps clear bowels, and other times thick ones;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes little, and others enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh covering it, this is unless by one of nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	That is to say, due to the scarcity of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	Or because of its nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Or due to the hard flesh within it, and on the lips, which prevents new flesh from forming;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or because there is too much bowel;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Where the flesh is porous, and the material of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not effective in treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where due to the corruption being a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where due to the characteristics of the region, digestion is slow, healing is delayed, and swelling occurs naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already demonstrated all these causes, their signs, and the treatments of medicine in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now is when I must inform you of the treatment for fistula, which is performed manually.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas occur in any part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that arise in major veins, arteries, nerves, at the anus, in the intestine, bladder, some ribs, the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And so until it returns to its proper place of origin, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of quick healing, and there is nothing but work and ignorance [involved].
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you are doubtful of its cure, and you wish to know it for sure, then take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, insert [the probe].
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a slender probe of lead, because lead can bend according to the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly probe it with instruments, then cleanse it by administering an enema through one of the openings, for moisture will flow from one opening to another and clean [the wound].
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then treat it skillfully to your ability, so that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and check whether it is completely severed, and carefully ask the patient about their pain when pressing with your hand, as well as where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And once you have truly located where it is, whether it is close to a joint or nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the areas I mentioned, treat it accordingly as I said before, and remove the fault and corrupted flesh that lies within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Then cure it until it is clean and healthy, and if the fistula is well-formed in a straight line, then you must treat it completely as best as you can. Then insert damp cloths soaked in healing medicines into it, pushing them down to the end of the fistula so that the medicine may corrode any remaining excess at its base.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply stimulating ointments to healthy flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize as we have said earlier, and if the bone is corrupted by the ulcer, amputate it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a wound or tumor does not harm your vital organs, as we have said before;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, remove the affected area until all corruption is gone, then treat it with stimulating substances to promote healing until it is cured.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and becomes swollen again as before, know that you have not reached deep enough.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore its place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	There may be another cause from which relief comes naturally.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small corrupted bone that you can grasp with tongs, remove it with the appropriate tool for this purpose. If there are multiple bones, extract them all at once and leave none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if moisture hinders you, and there is no risk of harm or danger, then cut through the moisture, flesh, and bone to free it.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, apply something that causes rotting to the wound, and let it rot around the bones until then the bone will be more easily extracted.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, clean only the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if a large part is corrupted, and it reaches the core of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	It must be cared for and cut away entirely until the corruption is removed, then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg caused by something within the body, such that matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, but there was no reason for opening [it] from outside.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the doctors in their madness worked so much on it that they opened up the abscesses and a lot of matter came out, and it became a fistula, with many apertures through which all the bowels and moisture of the body flowed.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	Many doctors tried to cure him for about two years, but none of them were wise in the art of surgery, until I was called upon. Upon examining his leg and seeing the treatments he had received as well as what flowed from those apertures, I observed that it came out through the apertures with a strong smell.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The body of the young man became red, and it had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, finding it rotten and perforated, with the rot spreading deep inside to the very bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away the part of the bone that appeared rotten, taking care to ensure there was no further rot beyond what I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time but it would not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	Later on, I restarted the process and reopened the wound to expose the bone as before, finding that the rot had continued into it. I scraped this away too, then removed it altogether, but was unable to make the place heal.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so as I was cutting around one palm's width of the bone, and it was torn throughout all its soft part, then I restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and joined swiftly, and there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of my fear of death from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For due to the blood evacuation he bled often, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone grew a hard tissue, which was well-formed and caused no harm or side effects whatsoever, either at present or later on.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a cord, and tie it to the end of the bone that is protruding, and instruct someone to pull it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another thicker flax rope over the flesh above the bone and tie it tightly while stretching the head (of the protruding bone), so that you draw away the corrupted flesh from underneath and uncover the flesh above where you wish to operate without cutting into the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a red hot iron or a table under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	you must take as much care as you can to see and feel the extent of the corruption, and check again once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted but does not open, and the corruption is either in the middle or on one side, you must uncover all of the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place the red hot iron underneath, and then cauterize from one side of the corruption to the other, and let there be a gap along its length as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut away the corrupted joint, and cauterize the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is present between two joints, there is no other remedy but to amputate.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, it is a very serious matter, but nonetheless you must inquire about this corrosion, how it presents itself.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	Clean it in every way you can, but be careful not to harm the veins or nerves.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	Know that there are many types of incisions and saws used to cut these bones, depending on the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, as well as their thickness, delicacy, size, smallness, and hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this, it is necessary to match each type of work with its corresponding tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that your work will show you the instrument or tool needed, according to your knowledge of this art and the signs of various diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Think carefully about the instrument or tool you require according to what is necessary.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may become dislocated either due to internal causes or external ones.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that ulceration with medicine and it does not improve, then you must amputate the limb up to where the ulcer originates so that the patient can escape death or the greater evil of member loss.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	The signs are that the limb turns black as if burned by fire and it may become darker still. The ulceration can spread from one member to another and then throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hurry to cut it, and if this is due to the sting of venomous beasts, such as a scorpion or snake, and if the corrosion is at the top of the finger, then cut it there, and do not allow any poison to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it has reached the hand, cut it at the joint so that the corrosion does not extend to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it has reached the arm, cut it with a knife.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	If it goes beyond the cut, it is death, and no strong remedy can be given other than a quantity of its antidote.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, then support the other joint after.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it affects the foot, support the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	If it goes up to the leg, support at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it goes above the knee, there is no other option but to leave the patient to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	The way to support or set the limb is that you bind it above and below, and have some assistants hold one end of the binding downwards, and others hold the other binding upwards, and you cut away the flesh between the two bindings with a spatula-like tool, until the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cover with cotton or silk, and place a linen cloth on either side so that the silk does not touch the healthy area, and no further injury or abscess occurs to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area immediately, or apply some restraining powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the affected limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you about what happened to a man with a sore foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a dark patch that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe, eventually covering the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after, the corrosion returned to his thumb, and he came to me. I applied resonant materials to it after purifying the body, but could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I wanted to cut off his hand, but I did not wish it, as I had hope of resonating with the material.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die because the man's health was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate and returned home, then hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have not described cauterization with hot irons because it is done differently elsewhere if there is need for it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At no time should an abscess appear in the flesh, and remain so long that it forms a large gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it swells up and bursts open, the pus escaping, leaving the wound raw like a hollow vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above it is as thin and delicate as fine linen, not extending down to the bone or nerve; such a disease is called 'ulcer', and not 'fistula'.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called a 'fistula'.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and let the skin be such that you cut this skin all around, especially when it is delicate, like a scarf;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not care about its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are worried that the skin will rot, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cut it thusly with a scalpel:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breasts are large, and the bowels that come from it have a foul odour, then administer an Egyptian medicine enema, which is made thusly:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take alum, oil, and litharge, equally, and put it to boil in a vessel over fire, until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take what you need from it, and mix it with water and honey, and flush the breast with an enema, and hold the aperture closed.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by pressing gently.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this several times until the breast is softened, and remove the pus.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And if you have performed an enema with ash water when this medicine is not available, and it is the case that you take wood ashes from vines, pour water over them, then strain them, and perform an enema until you know the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then perform an enema with water and honey where there is a small amount of powdered litharge.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	where you cleanse it with honey and mixed wine, for the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the blood flow.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the flesh is well cleansed, then clean it with what makes flesh grow in it, which is a definite plaster made of rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cleanse it with certain medications and ointments, whose properties I have described in the chapter on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the hole in the breast is small and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with an iron instrument a little bit, and put in it some Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, cut it and leave only enough space for the clyster to enter, and if the hole that emits feces is above, close it or lower where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the intestine is perforated, do not allow any food to enter.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cut the intestine as desired, arrange it in such a way that the intestine falls to its lowest point because when the intestine is perforated, do not allow any food to enter and if you cannot cut the intestine as desired, then prepare it accordingly.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the intestine runs slightly downwards, leaving nothing of the perforation.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to apply on the wound, and place them on a linen cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover as much of the surrounding area as possible with a hole in the chest that is wider than the first, then place soft ointment on another linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and apply it to the wound to ease the pain, and do not remove the large outer cloth for several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one on top of the chest wound should be frequently removed to alleviate the pain and inspect what comes out with the pain, whether it is poison or pus or blood or digestion, or undigestion.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and keep watch for the patient's pain levels and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in such a manner that you see nature emerging from the wound, then you know the chest is healing, and bring them close to health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then release it in the morning or on the third day; when you unwrap the wound, change to a new cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison lingers for a long time, do not despair of health, for healing is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men for whom healing of injuries comes late, and others who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if bowel movements become irregular after many days, know that the condition will not improve.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the healing is slow and prolonged, apply drying medications that are moist in substance but dry in nature, such as a definitive ointment containing a large proportion of vitriol. This will be the final medication applied.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take definitive ointment, and make it with rosehip oil, mixed equally in amount with old wine.
puis le confit et en use;	Then cook it and make use of it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And this same thing, when well cooked and thickened, is better without definite ointment present, or you can take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind it, and powder it with honey while it's still on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	Then glue it to a cloth and spread it over the chest, sometimes administering long-stemmed aristoloche and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour from vetch and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And make use of it with simple or composite medicines:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them, make powder from it, put on the honey I mentioned earlier, then apply it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is long, and not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has reached deep, and caused pressure on the bone, or hard tissue, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the fistula wound, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A panari is an abscess that arises beneath the fingernail or toenail of the hand or foot, or it may arise in other areas.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and not treated, an acute abscess develops, spreading pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and may even destroy the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it causes corrosion down to the bone, resulting in a foul-smelling pain, and the head of the finger or toe becomes enlarged, with a purple colour.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the classification, and the treatment does not improve its condition, then you must cut away all that which remains of the nail with an iron instrument, and afterwards cauterise the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterizations are a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to pierce it, wounding it, you must place a needle under the nail that is piercing the flesh, pushing it upwards, and carefully and gently cut away this flesh, then apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove all of it.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has reached the bone, cut it away, and pull hard, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, healing is not possible.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the finger is corrupted, cut it away from us, as it is said before, then treat until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is wounded, and kicked, and feels great pain, then you must first treat him with a cautery.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	cut the nail with a sharp spatula by slicing across it, and ensure that the cut does not go all the way through to the flesh beneath the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something that soothes it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the wrist joint of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two extra fingers that grow in some people's hands may be very fleshy, and sometimes there is also bone, and occasionally they have nails, and any of these can appear at the root of the knuckle or on various parts of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with a stiff finger cannot move it, but those who are born with a bend in the finger might be able to move it.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	For someone who is fleshy, the cut should be light in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	So you must be careful when cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the one that grows in the back of the hand, you must first cut away the surrounding flesh down to the bone, then cut out the bone with an appropriate saw, and treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the fingers together come through birth, or by sudden wounding, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Thus it is necessary that you cut that suture so that they may heal according to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or dampened cloths with rose oil so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you place between two pieces of fine lead until the flesh is sutured as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to anyone's palm of the hand, cut this suture as is necessary.
des vils	weakly.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are open wounds filled with melancholy humours that come from many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Thus you must administer to him sometimes purging of bile, and then heal with holy water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they cauterize it, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you raise the vein and draw all of it out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First immerse the leg in very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin, then raise the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places with a wide incision, then raise and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, until enough blood has come out according to the condition of the patient.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then let it settle, and instruct them to refrain from meat, consuming only black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Start the evacuation and incision again when the veins are full, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for this are as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Spread the patient's leg, if it is hairy, then immerse in a bath and bathe the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, heat it by the fire instead and then cover the area above the vein from the knee to the head of the leg or underneath the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then work the skin with an unciner, and flay the vein from each side, until it appears when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the vein aside, until it is raised from the skin, and then cut it with an unciner lightly, then cauterize in another place above by three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then flay the skin above the vein until it appears, then raise it with a hook, as you have done, and cut it with another unciner, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then make another cut, or more if you need to, then raise it and cut it with the finger of your foot, then pull it and lift it up until you reach the second cut.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract [the wound] layer by layer until it is completely clean, then treat it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot treat it and lift [the skin], insert a needle through the whole length with strong double thread, tie and pull it, place some beneath the line, turn your hand on either side until there is none left;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	Be careful that it does not split, because if it splits you cannot treat nor lift [the skin], and this harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated the whole [wound], place on it moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wound together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not sever it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	draw it out as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not slice but rather divides the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of thick curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein; but let it be large as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is entwined in the legs, in warm parts of the body where no grass or tree grows and on land that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And perhaps it arises elsewhere other than in the legs, and this occurs due to decay that comes from beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms arise within the body, engendered between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then its color changes, and the vein starts to protrude outwardly, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound opens, you must wrap around it a piece of lead measuring one and a half to two inches, tie it there, and leave the lead hanging from the leg. Every time exudate forms outside [the wound], rewrap it with the lead and retie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long [i.e., the exudate], cut away a part of it and rewrap with the remainder, but do not cut it at its root so that all comes out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it [i.e., the exudate], it will sink back into the flesh, causing an abscess and decay in that place, as well as a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary for it to be treated piece by piece up until the head, and not leave anything on the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein, when treated, measures five palms in length, or ten, and a man came to me whose vein emerged measuring ten palms long, and when you cut it, it ejects one ray of blood through an opening, and pierces down to the bottom, so that all comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	The matter inside it should be evacuated, and medicine promoting growth applied for several days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein is very narrow, especially when it appears at the ankle joint or foot, and a lot comes out through the opening, so that one should not cut it.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called 'ox disease' in our land, as it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body up and down, and one can feel its movement from member to member until it tears through the skin where it was, and dies.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is bred from the corruption of certain humours, just as worms, snakes, flatworms and Ascaris in the belly come about.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And one doubts its maliciousness because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, and then enters the eye, it may destroy it.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and treated, one cannot resist but when it is seen:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	one must therefore bind the place above and below with a strong tight bond, then press upon it and treat it forcefully, and if the pus is perfect within the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is to run into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming towards the eye or head near to it, then tightly hold underneath it the brow firmly, then press upon it, and treat it forcefully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And you must use purging of the body with laxative medicine to remove harmful humours and avoid eating meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that arises from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called 'vakirir' in our land, it is a pain that afflicts certain limbs and can move from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a sick woman, she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And soon after, I saw it rise up towards the shoulder like a worm, more than anything else, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that place, and settles in the shoulder, then spreads throughout the body, eventually reaching the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	It then returned again around the body, as I witnessed it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from limb to limb as I had never seen this illness behave in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had heard that many desired to move the pain from one place to another, but I never believed it until I saw it in this woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a slender body and her veins were exposed, which made this trapped wind visible.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it does not appear according to this reasoning for those who are delicate and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, bind it above and below tightly, then apply pressure until that windiness is forced back into place;
et cauterize le leu;	burn the area with a cautery;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you cannot see it with your own eyes, treat it as if raising blisters, using foul-smelling pills, such as those made from serpent's flesh, and similar others.
des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their variations include some with large points, others small, some are hairy, while yet others are smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and among them are those with two corners, some that have tongues, while yet others consist of multiple parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and this which falls on any limb falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member it begins, like the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you should be wary of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain, when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and if it touches the substance that is above the brain, is when there is darkness and stiffness in the eyes, and swelling and redness of eyelids, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and loss of understanding, and vomiting bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps it exits without fire from the nostrils or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps out white moist wound looking like pulsation, and also comes out like burnt flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, attend the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is close to the left nipple, and it feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know therefore without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrowhead has not pierced the lung is when there is no foam-free discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, and they breathe heavily and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the abdomen, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	It causes great pain and great difficulty breathing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls onto the stomach, perhaps something undigested of the meat comes out through the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls onto the belly, and no excrement comes out through the rectum, there is no hope in its treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, the urine jumps out and flows freely, and the patient feels intense pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the arm and collar bone, throat, shoulder, scapula, spine of the back, ribs, thigh, and legs; these limbs are protected according to many precautions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow fell on his neck into the root of the nose;
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I treated it from underneath the ear fat, and she was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in the game I extracted an arrow that had fallen into the fatty tissue of the eye beneath the conjunctiva below it. The arrowhead was embedded and could only be reached by its point towards the shaft, and the arrow itself was as long as a Turkish bow, with a light iron tip without barbs;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The eye healed, and no ill consequences befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with barbs;
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loosened the barbs, and manipulated it enough to extract it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew out an arrow from a man, which was lodged in his stomach or abdomen, and I thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, it did not change its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, manipulated it, and drew it out with force, and there was no ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has an arrow that fell on his back, and the wound is closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and it does not alter his natural condition nor cause any harm to his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, who has an arrow that fell on his face, and the wound is closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others of the same kind.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And draw out an arrow from the prince's nose that was lodged in it, and it had slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had been lodged there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched carefully throughout the entire nose, but did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a pricking sensation and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the point of the arrowhead. I applied an attractive and digestive poultice over the spot so that the flesh would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the shaft of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on immediately, and the wound healed quickly, but the patient remained ill for a long time, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	And he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a corrosive ointment to the wound immediately, until it opened up, and I probed it, feeling the tip of the arrow as it emerged.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I inserted a probe into the wound using that corrosive ointment, until the tip of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Over the course of four months, I gradually widened the end of the arrow until it protruded sufficiently from the wound for me to grasp with a pair of tongs, and I pulled it out bit by bit, but it would not come free.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then do not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments, until I took it one day with well-made forceps, according to that which its form will come in the end of this chapter, so that I drew it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care into what I do not say, because the book cannot possibly cover everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters know well very little about great things, and on what is presented to them and lacking, find new work, and a new instrument, for the understanding of strange occurrences which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows exit from members where they are stuck by two manners.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that jumps out through where it enters, is an arrow penetrating fleshy parts, and sometimes must be removed immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not need to be removed right away, leave it there until the flesh around it is rotten and the exit path has been prepared.
