et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is lodged in the bone and cannot exit, you leave it there for a few days and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if not, you must pierce around with an awl until the surrounding place is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes right up to one of the brain's ventricles, and some of the accidents I mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not extract it but leave it there until the swelling becomes equal after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the surface layer of bone, this means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains free of any ill effects for several days, then devise a means to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply lodged in this way and cannot be removed outwardly, then you administer theriacs all around as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in the body but cannot be seen, then probe all over it with a small stick.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot do so because of the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrowhead, and there is no bone, nerve or vein involved, then cut until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	Pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove the flesh that is attached to it on both sides as best you can, then break or bend the barbs so you can pull it free.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Be careful not to break the arrow as this would make its removal more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding tissue is rotten, then pull it out, for its extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, so administer that which we have said about wound treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And beware of incising the nerve and opening a vein, and set up means by which you may extract the arrow without danger, either soon or later, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help that there can be; and if you cannot do so, then place him as indicated by the signs which the wound reveals.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow which has entered from elsewhere or where nothing of it appears but the skin is swollen there if one sees or feels anything at all beneath:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Make an incision above it until the forceps will grasp it, then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it should spring away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot exit, leave her be for now, then resume extraction until it's complete.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is in her bone, push it through the entire shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrow is stuck, and you wish to administer pushing, provide a pointed instrument so that the tip of the arrow enters the hollow of the tool.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	then push it through thoroughly, and if the arrow is hollow, insert the pointed instrument within to ease its removal.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around it if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is stuck in her chest or belly or bladder or side and it's close to the surface and you can cut there, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard yourself from cutting the vein and nerve, then extract it, and finally stitch up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	until the treatment is clean.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to extract arrows resembles the beak of a bird, as you see here: [image]
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the amount of arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the wooden wedge is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here in this image: [image]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pincers for extracting and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins of the body common to all.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins from which one can be cured, of which sixteen are in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two "herbech" arteries located behind the ears;
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two visible temporal arteries;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in the two eyelids, which are called 'spirals';
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands which are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins which are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are called 'circles';
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins which are underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that we commonly heal are five in each arm;
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side, and laymen call it 'the head vein';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The means is called "faste", and it consists of the cephalic and basilic [veins], which lay people call the "heart vein".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilic vein is found on the right side, and lay people call it the "abdominal vein", and it lies above the muscle, and it is through this that one is healed, as it clearly appears near the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	The cephalic vein is the one that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	In the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is located beneath the arch of the left foot, and the second is the saphenous vein which is at the right ankle;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse", that is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic colds and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of bleeding is such that you raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then hold the patient's neck with a strap so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	close your fingers to your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, make an incision there.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein until you reach bone. Then lift your hand so that all of the vein upstream is exposed. Cut through both skin and vein in one incision across two fingers' breadth, and allow blood to flow freely as long as you wish.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then restrain it and bind it tight until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	I have already mentioned the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for long-lasting migraines, persistent eye infections and acute watering of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	The quality of bleeding should be as follows:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And let the patient strain their neck until the two veins are clearly visible.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	He will feel the pulse below your thumb, and then make an incision there.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then place your heart over the vein above your index finger, push the lancet underneath and lift up the vein and skin as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your needs.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient's arm and place your finger over the vein for an hour before covering it with cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then bind it tightly, leaving it like this until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	We have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is just as valuable as the bleeding of the cerebral [vein] for ancient diseases of the face and for migraine and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it so much that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called 'fosseur', of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or another object, and let out as much blood as you wish;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein so that it is secure but not too tight, without constricting the entire hand at once.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the flames must not be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And let the wound be crooked, for the bone is close by, and perhaps it will break the flame if it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples aids the eyes, and treats inflammation, redness, and swelling in the eye, as well as diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient stretches their neck by twisting with a cord, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then wound it, and let the wound be transverse, slightly shorter than the length of the flame, and somewhat wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is delicate, perhaps it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then drain out the blood until you have what you need, then bind it with cotton, and wrap it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Opening the vein in the nose is good for fever, sudden headache, and illnesses of the face such as migraine and facial redness, especially when it is long-lasting.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of this bloodletting is that the patient should stiffen their neck, then strain their nose with your left hand, and take the delicate long flame, inserting it between the two nostrils where the vein does not open fully, and the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two arteries helps with narrowing the throat, and in beginning of inflammation, and in many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and tumors;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient stretches their neck beneath one another, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the masters be above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein from the long side a little broadly, then draw out blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then remake it on the other vein, untie the bandage, and hold all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not suffocate.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of veins on the upper lip helps with glue in the mouth and gum corruption, and fissures of lips and nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the healing process require you to have the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip, and the other is on the left; they can be recognized by being darker in color and having small dark veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Treat both of them and if you cannot recognize or are in doubt about which to treat, then cauterize the larger one on each side; do this also for the two veins that are above and below as it is a similar process.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of veins below the tongue is aided after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it helps with narrowing in the throat, and diseases of the eye, and mouth ailments.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeder are such that the patient knows to place their hands in front of the sun, and lift their tongue, and look beneath each side for a dark vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	bleed one and the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where they are pierced with a very sharp, wide-mouthed lancet or a subtle olivewood one as keen blades, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open up narrow veins filled with dense, visible blood, and those that contain thick and cloudy blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	it is more pointed and slender, and it is for bleeding the delicate veins where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, aids in treating diseases below the throat, and in the neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And the bleeder must bleed gently, being careful of the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he strikes the artery, causing blood to flow out, it must be stanched as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And one must not pinch the flame, but cut it like a thread.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, you must remove it, and change to another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Or if you desire any ray of it, or you heal in its place the vein among the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	It opens clearly
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And apply the flame to the thread, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of incision, it is necessary that you first pull out the arm, until you touch the site so that you recognize the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Sign the place of incision, then bind the arm, and open the vein below with a knife.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	Be careful not to wound the artery when you see the place swell, for that is the artery.
eschui la donques.	Avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and press your finger there for some time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	If the arm is bound, leave it so, and do not move the patient's arm.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And leave it to fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not staunched, and you faint, and there are no medical professionals present, then cut the artery that is open, as it leads to the head.
et estainche li sans.	And staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig bark, split it, then take one half and bind it firmly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the blood is staunched, that's good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it is not, then treat as mentioned before with powders that staunch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the binding is not severe in many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bloodletting of the vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from both above the head and below the body, for it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And the bloodletter must take care not to go too deep, lest they hit the nerve below, and if it is struck and swells, the bleeding will be severe, and perhaps they cannot stanch it;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve often lies close to the surface, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you must bleed it with a slender instrument;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And avoid the nerve with your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make a long cut to open it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding of the cephalic vein is beneficial, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed by piercing with an olive twig or a myrtle twig, for it is the safest of all veins, as it has neither nerve nor artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must seek the lightest spot, and not do much harm if one misses the first time, and then begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance the spot swells in some men when one misses the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it should not be used except to preserve health and prevent future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the incision be made on one of the three veins located at the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and if one must bleed at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed either the first or third day, two to three hours after midday.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The time for administering bleeding is not fixed but whenever required, day or night, at all hours and any time.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And one should not bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a pregnant woman within the first four months and up to seven months of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to be bled who are aged over sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it is done, one must first cleanse the bowels with a light clyster if there is an abundance of retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful and superfluous waste from the intestines which are detrimental to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One should not be bled if they are too full of meat or intoxicated until such time as these conditions have passed nor is it suitable for those who suffer from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one wishes to be bled after suffering from violent abdominal pain, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse, exertion or labor, lack of sleep and fasting and for those who have no strength left in them due to injury or illness...
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly reduce the humours, if the blood is thick, through food, drink, and medicine, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin out the blood, and treat yourself for the pain around the third part of your body, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And protect yourself that day from work, exertion, lustfulness, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And remain still and cheerful, and have the surgeon stand higher than you when treating you, and rub your arm twice or thrice before he tightens the ligature moderately, for if it is too tight or narrow, blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then you rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and they can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the wound with a little old oil, and place your left index finger on that vein beneath the site, slightly higher than where you wish to make the incision, so as not to allow the blood to escape and cause failure in the procedure.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like cords when incised, and for such cases which are full of windiness, so that when you place the knife upon them, it retracts from the flame and cannot open the vein, thus it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if you open the vein too much, then the wound is too narrow; for this reason, the surgeon must be mindful of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the wound opens up for the first time, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, begin again somewhat below that place or above it, if the areas are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the areas are swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps there will be hot abscesses arising from this situation.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter the bath, then restart the incision if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the hole is small and blood flows out delicately, causing you to doubt that it will not come out in sufficient quantity as desired, then press firmly on the same hole with all your flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little quickly, rather than when the flesh is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh swollen, do not reopen the wound, and put a little oil liniment on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is soothing in this place where the oil belongs;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil liniment in every wound that you treat for veins, to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing is astringent and bows when placed on the flesh;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so subtly does the blood separate and disperse when it is too profuse.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when there has been no previous bleeding other than the opening of the vein this time or the incision is small, you must act quickly and apply a sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the wound for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, you should do this, and if it remains in place for a few days without any blackness or greenness appearing, then it will not harm them.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see this, apply something made from aloe or myrrh dissolved in calamint juice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and appearance occur at the bleeding of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft when compressed by the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, ensure you do not put anything on it that we have mentioned, for perhaps the artery will burst.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But apply a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Draw out the blood according to its quantity and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see that it is thick, leave it so until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make the wound larger, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	For one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is suitable to bleed them often in small amounts, and you must bleed by slicing across, not pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding lengthwise or widthwise.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body needs bleeding, give them moist bread soaked in pomegranate juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If they are hot-tempered, draw three or four times as much blood. If they have a cold constitution, feed them moist bread soaked in spiced syrup, either of mushed grapes or honey with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, well scented.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the operation after a great loss of blood, it is necessary that he inhales beef broth, and subtle scented syrup, and uses other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for venous evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed out his arm, and operate another time, it is necessary that when he is weakened by great bleeding, he bleeds little by little according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm after the first operation, and has a strong constitution, it is recommended that he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to bleed from another part of the body, it must be done on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood within his body which is already heated, and it causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If one must drain a large quantity, then the opening should be enlarged until it yields in padding.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then ensure all the conditions for healing are right, and place your hand on his pulse as he heals, so death does not come to the padding, and this happens many times when healers are neglectful.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not appropriate when you wish to release the arm, and make blood come out a second time, if the opening is closed, that you press heavily upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he bends his arm, make him extend it forcefully, for this would be wrong.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Where you prick it with the tip of a flame, until the frozen blood escapes from the vein, put on some wool soaked in warm water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then drain it from the same place, or from another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is drained in place of the one on the head because it is composed [of two].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of cauterization is for the patient to immerse their hand in hot water until the nails are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then bind it gently so the vein appears clearly, then cauterize across its width, not from side to side nor lengthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And if the wound is wide and it must be cauterized close to the joint of the hand, and blood cannot escape, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, do not plunge the hand into warm water, for one plunges it more often during winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the incision of this vein is safer than all other veins as it has neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The incision of the basilica vein in the right hand is valuable for all ailments related to the liver, and this is how it should be done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Immerse the hand, and plunge it into warm water until the vein becomes swollen so that it may be seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the incision is made lengthwise, and you cut across it completely, it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are all beneath, denuded of flesh, and then return the hand to warm water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled from the blood as much as is necessary for you, put oil and linen on the vein to weld the wound, and do so with each ray.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of the one on the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you regarding the right [hand].
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The draining of the spleen is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments in the thighs and legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his cure is such that the patient soaks their foot in warm water and rubs it over the vein until it perishes, then binds it above the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is in the ankle, and from there up the leg it goes very much downhill;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat it then where the slope is steepest, or at the ankle, whichever moves better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the leg, beware of the nerves which are beneath, and treat it across as well, just like when cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, return the foot to the water, and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you miss the wound the first time, try again a little above it, for the skin is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise for the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is found at the back of the ankle, and its incision relieves pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his wound is such that the patient enters the bath, and presses down on the ankle for four days by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, then treat the wound in all ways that you can, and traverse it.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to cut it, for the skin is salty, and it is very sensitive for most people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then press any point of his foot which protrudes at the back or towards the small toe, and be cautious of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	Make sure to remove any blood that is flowing until you see it stop, then untie the binding and apply cotton, pressing down on it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping incisions.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horn, or brass, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done in two ways.
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping method that does not involve wounding is done in two ways.
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Where there's fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and venting, which is done by striking and by bloodletting in fourteen places of the body, one being entirely at rest at the top - the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and another is midway on the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others at either side of the collarbone;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cups over both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and cupping glasses on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and cups over both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cups for both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cups for both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw any blood, only taking small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and thus it does not weaken one at all, unlike bleeding of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, nor with fire or without fire, in any illness caused by overeating until the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness cupping must be done, or for habit's sake, we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and in between at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to be cupped, have such heavy heads.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And for those who find fullness and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkening of the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And for those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongues, and spit up blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are those who dream and see blood, wounds, death, and similar things during the night.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is towards the middle of the month, we order that they be cupped after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Bloodletting from the nose helps with the splitting headache that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuating all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the head artery, and one must not use it for someone with a cold constitution or who has catarrh, as it causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, one must not use it on the elderly or those with cold ailments in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who bleed often become forgetful, so the cupping glass should be placed a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping in the middle of the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and basilic arteries, and for this reason, it aids in narrowing the chest, and in splitting the channel of the lungs, and in coughing, and in fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be applied briefly, for if it holds too firmly, it causes loss of memory or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the two collarbones is beneficial for head pains, eye ailments, migraines, choking sensations, tooth root pain, and it sits at the place where the basilic vein arises.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the patient to extend their arm fully for measurement, taking care not to constrict the artery and avoiding any excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation below the chin is beneficial for mouth ailments, such as gum infections, and similar diseases that affect the oral cavity.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is located at the place where the veins of the two lips arise.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventousation of the shoulders helps with illnesses brought about by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilation of the armpits is just as valuable as that of the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from those larger veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the healer not to make it too perfect, for the bone is bare of flesh, and beneath are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttocks is useful for hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases below, and it must be large and made of brass, requiring good traction;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps, if it were thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs heal evidently, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are useful for old pains of the kidneys, bladder, and uterus, and relieve flowers.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are located at the two sophens, and the two ankles; yet they weaken the body over time, and bring about fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cup is as follows: place it first on an empty area, suck vigorously, put it quickly, move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the redness of blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then incise, and put back the cups, and take care with the condition of bodies, for there are those who have tough flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	you should only strike once, and make large wounds, with deep punctures.
et suce legierement.	And suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, it is necessary to strike a third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to draw out thick blood gradually, we only strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we often restart.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is dense, strike it thoroughly, and finish by piercing the heart suddenly; this is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and narrow veins, you must oil the cupping glasses with an aperitive and dissolving ointment.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is linseed oil, violet oil, sweet almond oil or cucumber seed oil
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is to heal, use watercress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the wound has tender flesh and large pores, do not apply oil but wash it after the fomentation with rosewater, or cold water, or black nightshade water, or squash water, or china root water, or any similar solution.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, rise easily with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar solutions.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive swellings should rise with old wine, or an infusion of salt water, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar remedies.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not advisable to bloodlet with cupping before the bath or during the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and one should not sleep after cupping therapy, it is necessary to stay awake both when one needs to be cupped and during the treatment itself.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take care if the patient is choleric, and if their blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	they should eat cold things like pomegranates, endive, lettuce, and similar foods;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat small amounts of food, lean meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with a cold constitution, take honey syrup and drink aromatic medium wine, which is neither old nor new, eat little, and consume small portions of food, small birds, and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is cupped, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men treacle or musk once before or after the cupping to comfort their main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be refined, but it is not appropriate for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are applied without injury are those placed over the liver, and over the breast, podagra, and the abdomen, groin, kidneys, and hip, because these members cannot bear to be wounded there, nor is it done for anything but to draw blood from member to member, just as we put them on nipples when a child suckles;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity from the member, just as we apply cups to the abdomen and groin to reduce the size of the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain when there is concretion or stone, as it perhaps extracts the concretion by its attractive virtue, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus it does when applied over the liver and abdomen in cases of retained flatulence, these cups are administered empty to simply draw out.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Sometimes they are administered with fire and sometimes filled with warm water, as in cases of pleurisy, and one may fill the cup with warm water alone or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of administering fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	It is two fingers wide and half a palm deep with a small hole in the middle, large enough for a needle to pass through, and it is made of soft copper so as not to injure the patient when applied to the limb. 
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And it has a metal bar running across the middle, either copper or iron, to hold a lit taper and there are various sizes of cups, large and small, depending on the illness and the constitution of those who use them. 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For children's cupping glasses are different from those of adults, and those of thin people from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one should place this cupping glass on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the candle of wax or tallow and place it inside the cupping glass through the hole that is in the glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it on the limb, with your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, you can let out the vapour, and remove the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take the tallow again as before, and repeat this often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping treatment administered for pleurisy, it is completely hollow and has no tube or opening, and it should only be applied when it is full of water, and placed directly on the affected limb.
et c’est li forme:	and its shape is thus:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not applied to any limb where one cannot place a cup due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And on the bare skin of these places if any, such as fingers or toes, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	The quality of use is such that when you find suction cups filled with clean, odourless water, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them overnight in fresh water until they are tender, and have nothing in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then bleed the patient using veins and cups, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply leeches;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they become full and fall off, if it is a place where cups can be applied, apply them, because this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the area with ease, then water, very well, and then bandage it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area bleeds excessively after the application of leeches, dampen a linen cloth with cold water and place it on top until the bleeding stops.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood has multiplied, apply ground vitriol to warts or similar things, until it is dried out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	where you place half of a peeled broad bean, leaving it until it dries up in the air will staunch the bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you require more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches will not attach themselves, rub the place of fresh blood with a needle until blood appears and then put them on: immediately upon sensing the blood they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are defecating, apply a powder of aloes and ground sel or ashes on them, and they will drop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here we have the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu'il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n'en lurent;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason knowledge is lacking in our land, because I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated patients and gained experience, and through the habits of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within it, and abbreviated at the end, showing clearly the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we state in the prologue of this book the main points and the chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains focused on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage occurs to anyone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on both sides if nothing else prevents it, such as frailty of body, infants, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	Whether the weather is too hot, or far too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	Eat cold foods, such as cold porridge and goat cheese, but avoid any wine or greasy meats. Do not overindulge in too much meat that fills the veins with blood until you are certain there is no risk of a hot abscess or spreading matter to the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient relapses, return them to their initial management.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one feeds the patient with meats that have high nutritional value and are rich in fat, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, eggs, chicken feet, cow stomach, duck eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar foods.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For if too much nutrition is taken, the healing process can be hindered and the fracture may occur again sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Understand that broken bones in the elderly and frail cannot be properly reset or healed according to their natural drying process for limb recovery. Nor can those who are too young, such as small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But have no fear, reset over the broken bone with large clamps that grip and bring the limb together, so it is strong as before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not move it at all from its position, for this reason you must nourish with large pieces of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm, or the leg, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways fractures can occur.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is fracture that requires splinting, and another by sharpening, just like the cut of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if fracture with wound, and fracture with just a slight crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each method have its tools and proper instruments in the restoration, according to what memory brings to mind when needed.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the bone is known to be broken when it is twisted out of place and obvious from the outside, with a sound when pressed by hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or sound upon touch, and the patient feels little pain, then there is likely no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may well be a twist, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow here, and then hold it firmly yet gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes through lengthwise, and where the two parts are separated, they must now be put back together equally, otherwise hot abscesses will form there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses do come about, leave them alone for one day until the abscess is calmed down;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it equal to the stumps that you can find lightly and cleanly, and know that its restoration is easier than those where parts are missing.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it firmly, just as one should do afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it out in two directions, whether it is an arm or foot, or with your hand if it's one of the smaller limbs, or with two cords, or with one cord and use your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	Place the limb according to its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the member are disjointed, you bring them together by all means possible towards their joints as much as you can, and be careful not to cause any injury or pain to the patient through your work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	Adjust the two ends of the bones well according to their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	Feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not yet aligned properly:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it heals well, and is not held too tight or pressed so much that causes hot abscesses and contractions in the limb as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at the right stage, chastise the patient well so they do not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, or turning around, or in any other way.
