et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Ensure that the limb is well secured so they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when they feel no pain, it is not yet ready, and must be put in such a position that they do not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And take care that it is put correctly, without any twisting when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	The qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, length, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as arms, legs, and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	you should wrap it in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are larger, such as thighs and calves:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	you should wrap it in a wide and firm bandage because the broad bandages embrace the whole large member and hold it tightly from all sides so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind it with light pads, three or four turns according to the member, and tighten your hand slightly over all the bandage then go above the break and tighten less so that the breakage can move a little away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, so much that you grasp a large part of the healthy place, then take another ligament and turn again immediately onto the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the lower part of the break and hold it moderately, neither too hard nor too soft, as we have said in the first passage above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the ligaments linen or soft cloth, so that it is all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, put on soothing hot poultices that reduce the abscess and the swelling, and leave them there for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain it over your sieves, and let them be half of a thick cane cut carefully, or of the wood used to make handles, or of palm ribs, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the sieve one places over the broken bone be slightly larger and broader than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is necessary for the member, be it small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then strain over the sieves just as you have done with the first layer, then bind above it with thread accordingly, just like in the first layer on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the narrower part is above, the wider below;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the thread must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and it should be made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted flax cords, and this is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have more than two finger widths between each strand.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the bones of the stars after the restriction in their veins, place beneath them pads of linen or woolen dressings so they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by broken ribs, and the heart is ruptured, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to reset all broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it should not be bound with strands until after five or seven days, or more depending on your assessment of the severity of the abscess that has developed;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and sprains;
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and make this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common way of making a healing plaster for various fractures, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of making a healing plaster for fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take 1 lb of apricots, myrrh, nettle, galangal, asafoetida, and gum Arabic; then add 10 lbs.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, take 5 lbs.
alechil VIIII З.;	Alechil (an herb used for its medicinal properties), take 9 lbs.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	et in powder form, and mix it with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the man's complexion is warm, then apply this plaster, for it has good ingredients and quickly restores broken bones, aiding many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another type of plaster that is useful for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mullein and viscum, 10 each;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, 9 each;
acaice VI З.;	acacia, 6;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	armenian bole, 10; grind it well and mix with water or egg white, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another kind of poultice for joints and bones that have moved out of place, it soothes the emerging pain, softens hardened bone tissue, and treats fractures.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take some new linen cloth, soak it in warm water and oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [the bone], but it is good to ease a hot abscess, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another type of poultice that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and earth-apple leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of a plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remainder of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violets' flowers, vetches flour, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them together, mix with wine, if the limb is hot, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water; and apply this.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another plaster method stronger than the first one for when a persistent abscess affects limb restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind it, and mix it with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, depending on the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put a broken limb together to restore its strength with anything other than wax and oil; he also says it must be neither too soft nor hard but between the two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one must place on the broken limb, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another type of plaster that is effective for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and chopped men's hair, or bird feathers, and viscum, and mix them evenly with glue, then grind these into a plaster and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then you must undo the binding a little after, taking care that the patient feels no pain and that the bone has not moved out of place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	Do not undo it by hand if dry.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place or itching occurs, or swelling or restlessness is felt, then hasten and undo it now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light fabric, and sea sponge moistened, immerse in water, then lift the area until itching ceases, and pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place dry wool soaked in water or rose oil above, and bind with linen, until you are sure the abscess is warm.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflamed limb, and pain should be gone, then resume gentle binding with a small amount of plaster, do not bind as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has drained and the redness, pain, and swelling have all gone, and you need to use poultices and bandages, then start it over again just as you did originally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb as we have said, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes it is left for XX days, as seen, until the fracture heals, and the adjustment of the flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Therefore, restrain it more than before, and thicken its meat, as I said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that no nourishment can come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Moisten it with warm water each time you undo it, every third day, and loosen the binding slightly;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this treatment, nourishment is cut off to the limb, and amends the mistake of those foolish surgeons, who reset the limb crookedly;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is harmful, and such work is fearful; I see no other option than to leave it and operate correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the diverse manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many types of fractures exist, and they present in various forms; the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the shaft pierces and removes all bone down to the soft tissue beneath the bone, just as an axe or wooden club would do.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And so this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword chops the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And there are wounds from these two types of fractures, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded impact, or cracks due to stone fragments, or falling on stones, or similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which reaches the membrane beneath the bone or above it on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is as thin as a hair, responding to the bone with a small fracture, and thus it is called a "capillary" break.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a blow from stone or by falling, or any similar thing that drives bone inward, and its edges are split like those of cauldrons when hammerers strike them.
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone enters within it.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those with moist or soft bones in the head, such as children's heads.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these types of fractures that small fragments are dislodged, like stars.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak to him/her in his/her place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We know all kinds of fractures through their deformity, and we inquire about them by touch, and from the corrupt flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is understood by the fact that when you uncover the bone and rub it repeatedly, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take heed of the patient's symptoms, and if you see no ill symptom, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, fainting, feverishness, chills, redness around the eyes, and other similar conditions in many cases, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no alarming symptom and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the membrane beneath the bone become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, you must split the fractured part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you take the sick person's head without pity, and uncover the bone in every possible way, and over the wound's surface as gently as possible, and if bleeding occurs upon uncovering the bone or pus comes from the abscess, then there is help for what must be done, and it is necessary to fill the place with damp rags moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess has healed, and be sure there is no further bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then start by removing flesh around the bone, and this is done in two ways according to their work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One way is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is that you make multiple different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of hard iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and you work lightly so as not to harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	If the bone is hard and strong, then you must drill around it rather than cutting into it with knives or iron rods, so as not to penetrate too far beyond the skull, and there should be a ridge or circle above the point, which stops the tip from passing through.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several of these, so that each one comes into place according to the type of bone, so that you have drills for all your tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality required to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then remove the drill slightly further away and repeat this process all around, then use the scalpels to cut the space of the bone that is between the perforations, doing so as finely and gently as you can, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand or any of the instruments such as forceps or pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And make sure you do not touch the brain or the sciatic nerve.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you remove the remaining splinter with an instrument similar to a small scalpel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other scalpels.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there is any leftover small bone or scales, remove them lightly with one of the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	The other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is more gentle.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And press it very firmly, for this is his instruction.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first expose a part of the bone where the fracture appears, so that when you have uncovered this area, you will place underneath the head of this lens-shaped instrument; and here is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, as the blade is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edges face towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike gently with a small mallet on top, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and take great care of the membrane below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, remove it gently, as you can lift it without causing harm or fear of injury.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	Et if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the marrow, and the bone is merely cut above, with small pieces present, you must smooth out this roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in varying quantities, to apply appropriately in each place according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large rasps first, then finer ones, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-fine cuts and subtle fractures, you must adjust your approach according to its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be fully answered by someone who has merely studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, you must take a piece of linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, dampen it with rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another piece of cloth doubled over twice or three times, dampen it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	do this as lightly as you can to avoid damaging the wound, then apply another bandage on top without tightening it too much so that it only holds the cloths in place.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess is cooled down, then remove the bandage and apply medicine such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, aristologist remedies, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer it immediately with mild medicines without any biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is always clean, leaving no ointment nor allowing any pus to accumulate, for when pus gathers on the brain membrane, it runs and putrefies, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you apply biting substances onto it, they corrode from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening appears only due to the medicine applied, and that it has such a property, you must take one part honey, three parts rose oil, and mix in a small piece of linen cloth, then place this onto the wound;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the physician proceed with treatments as necessary, until healing is complete.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the collarbone are broken or just one, for there are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	The broken end is cartilaginous and does not break further; it only becomes dislodged or twisted, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the collarbone's gap and align that break within your index finger so it fits snugly, then gently push from outside until the collarbone regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do this gently, and wait for the patient to indicate no pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nose and cannot be properly set with fingers alone, you must put a stick, slightly thicker than a finger, equal to the head of the shoulder bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another just like it, and restore the first one as soon as possible on the same day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after seven or ten days, when the hot abscess is pacified, then place on the head of the nose tented linen bandages if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you place another on the other side, if there is a fracture there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bits of cloth with butter, changing them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem good to me, but they must be moistened with a mixture of egg white and flour paste;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then let the tent remain, until the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes goose quills are inserted in place of tents, and if there is soft cloth around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient blows through it.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form in the nose while you are working, put some wax ointment or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a piece of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if no abscess forms there, apply an external plaster made of bran flour, incense powder, and egg white, then put on light dressings, but do not tie the quill.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	If the quill's fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments for this purpose, then clean the wound, treat it with appropriate dressings and ointments, and apply plasters.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the nose, treat it with tents, and place thin planks of wood inside until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	From a fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured sideways, and there are no external wounds, and the fracture is only outwards, without splitting it in two, unless the edges overlap slightly inside, one may easily detect this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	You must, if the fracture is on the right side, insert your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left jawbone, insert your right index finger and gently push the broken part inside, then adjust it with the other hand from outside, ensuring it is aligned.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated in two, you must administer traction on both sides until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	If there is movement or a crack in the teeth, secure them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply wax to the broken jawbone and cover it with a doubled piece of cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on the cloth a large well-made star or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it as firmly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meat dishes.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put an ointment on top, made from mill dust with plenty of egg or sesame seed flour, after you have removed the crust.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put light woolen ointment on top, and if the ointments harden, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess arises, so treat it as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, treat it as long as no part of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so delicately to remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have removed all the displaced pieces and there are no remnants left, clean the wound, if it is wide, then apply suitable dressings to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	Forceps.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forearm breaks in multiple places towards the front, near the shoulder, and this fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Where it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and this is the easiest to reset.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture accompanied by a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the treatment is as follows when the fracture occurs without an accompanying wound: have two assistants where one holds the shoulder with the broken forearm while...
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and let the other stretch the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place your two hands evenly on the fracture, so that its shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor conclusion (to it).
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to further extend it, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let its size be according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	stretch and lift the arm, holding the sphere in your hand, so that you can evenly place the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out because it is too deep, due to that reason, the patient must often lie on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow beneath their shoulder, and have your assistants push the shoulder downwards so that the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then adjust the fracture with your two hands, and if you find it misaligned, you must cut above it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then cut it with one of your incising tools.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but apply the force beneath this instrument to secure the skin flap.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, without teeth, and is as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you can see, with one wide and the other narrow, just like the gap in the wound that was created when you drew out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are confident of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the gap is small or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with lint and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a warm abscess appears, dampen a cloth with rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and uncut, is that you place on the bone a plaster made with mill powder and egg white, and put light dressings on top, and place a sphere beneath the pillow if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage, one palm-width in width, then place two layers of cloth on the dressings and plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender stick three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	Place the stick over the fracture, and wind the bandage around the neck, beneath the healthy shoulder, and underneath the injured shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the marrow has not moved from above the broken bone, then encourage it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain them again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under their shoulder when they sleep, to raise the shoulder upwards.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	this lightens the fracture of the collarbone due to the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind their arm to the neck and do not release it unless some unfortunate event happens until 20 days pass.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and restrain them again, leaving them in this way until they are healed.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it is restored most often within twenty-eight days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For a broken shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Soon it happens that the shoulder dislocates from its wide or middle position, and is not set back into place through touch alone;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you fix it according to the shape of its break, and reset it following its natural form, in any way that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the place powder of mill with abundance of egg, and light tapestries, and place over it a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place on top a wide and thin pillow, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there is thinning of the pillow in any part of the shoulder, fill it with flax tapestries so that the pillow remains even;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then hold it firmly with a large bandage all around, so that the star cannot move from its place, and check the binding each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it softens, bind it again, and keep the star level if it has moved from its place, and have the patient lie on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is healed in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is complete, you may unbind it, and be certain, for it is not light bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of the bone protrudes before and pierces beneath the heart, they should do as follows: remove it and treat any abscess with cauterization, as we have mentioned for fractures previously.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the humerus...
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The foot is sometimes broken in half, but this occurs rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the outer edge.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards and causes great pain for the patient due to a lack of alignment, resulting in shaking and trembling movements. Sometimes they vomit blood and one can see the ends of the bone through the skin, which indicates a severe fracture.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on their back, and you place a cushion between their shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the sides of the two ribs with your hands, and carefully align it evenly in every way possible, until the bone structure is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then apply plaster and fine cotton wool soaked in thin brine of salt, or another light wood, and wrap it with a cloth, binding it to the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And wrap the bandage around the back in a circular motion, tightening it gently, and loosen and retighten every hour, if it softens, then tighten again;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it needs to be released due to corrosion or itching that arises in the place, or pain or abscess, hasten and release it, remove the plaster, and address what has come up regarding treatment methods.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the plaster, and hold it tight until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the rib fracture occurs only in the thick part behind the back and at the head inside, and it bends only because they are fragile.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one feels it well during examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and restrain with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture tilts inwards, the patient feels great pain and stabbing, like a stitch, as the bone pierces the membrane.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it causes severe pain, with violent vomiting of large clumps of blood, which is an immediate danger; the old people have applied great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say it is necessary to administer foods that bloat the belly in order to push the rupture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless heat has already come to the abscess.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some of you may say to put cups on the spot to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the cup will draw out excess humours to the spot due to its weak suction.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say to cover the site with damp wool in warm oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the length around, then be cured by the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pressing against the tissue, and there is doubt in the patient's mind, then it is necessary to make an incision over the location of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument beneath to protect the lung.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, and pull it gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if hot abscesses develop, apply moist rags soaked in rose oil on the affected area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the area prone to abscesses regularly, ensuring it lies constantly on its side where necessary until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Regarding the broken neck...
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the neck, and this may cause it to bend.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will heal or not, take note: if you see their hands become soft, swollen, and lifeless, unable to move or stretch, and when pricked with a needle, there is no sensation.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many positions, and if they feel better when you move them and apply pressure, know that the bone's socket is saved, and the patient can be cured with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	If a similar issue arises in the spine of the back and you wish to ascertain whether it is healed or not, observe if the feet are weakened, and if there are accidents involving the hands, and on the back watch for windiness and involuntary defecation.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when he has been placed supine on his belly, there is involuntary defecation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and wants to mount, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if you do not treat it well.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, then the matter is more trivial.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you spread on it warm oil of roses or yolk of egg, until it is soothed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then apply one of the soothing and drying plasters, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And let him not sleep on that part of his body where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dislodged, it is necessary to cut above the heart.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment and freshen the flesh until it heals.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', push it with your left hand's palm until it is level with the other hand's power, then apply a plaster and a bandage over it, if you need to.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then restrain it, and if there is any dislodged bone inside, take it out through the wound, then treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if so, there is no great diminution at the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and while it is long, and bent backwards, and comes to the patient pain in place, and pricking, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, so that you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and feel where the fracture is and what its shape is;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is at the head only, make this fracture even, so that it has its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise or inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their belly so that you can see this break clearly to restore it.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, put on an emplastron, then place a stick of wood or heartwood over it, and bind the fracture so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the space under the ribs, so that the strap is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if hot abscesses arise there, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are soothed, and apply what we have previously mentioned.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	then return to the restoration, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad incident;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	On the fracture of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistants are those located between the armpit and the top of the shoulder, and if they are broken, one must restore them according to one of two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take one wooden rod with an average thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	Et tie the two shoulders with two bindings, lift them upwards, and place the patient on a seat.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then throw the broken arm onto the wood until it reaches the armpit, and place in the middle a curved piece of wood, then lift something heavy where the ministers extend downwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the splint so that it breaks evenly with their hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to lift the patient onto their back and bind their hand to their neck; command two assistants to hold what is above the break with their hands joined together, while another holds below at all points of the binding, stretching each part as required.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, tighten the cord below the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the assistants to their respective positions.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, you should place one binding underneath the armpit, and the other towards the neck, underneath the splint.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	Also, if the break is towards the neck, you should place one binding lightly and without force, so that the splint sits evenly on the spot and against the neck.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the fracture evenly as it ought to be, holding it still if no abscesses come about.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do appear, don't hold it still for seven days, and apply moist woolen cloth with rose oil until the abscesses are soothed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it still again, and the way to do so is to place a poultice on the fracture, then bring the arm over the shoulder, and put your hand on their shoulder or chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And wrap it with a cloth, holding it still over the shoulder and arm so that the arm is held in place like a star, unless something prevents this or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint over the fracture, allowing one finger width of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to extend three fingers on either side of the break.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then tighten the splints on top of one another, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter about fractures, tightening them more firmly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the placement of the splints and their tightness, as we have said, during the work of restoring the broken limb, and you suspect an abscess may form due to heat, leave it bound until the seventh day, just as we mentioned.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then inspect every three days the bandage, that no itching or swelling may arise in the place, nor nourishment come to the member because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment succeeds, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none of these accidents occur, do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands resting on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	place under the shoulder a cushion filled with wool evenly, and check every hour during the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not change, nor the bandage become loose.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it succeeds due to the virtue of medicine, give them the diet we previously mentioned, ensuring that their food is very refined.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, let it be big.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be treated within forty days overall;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it must be loosened and administered with baths and medicinal ointments to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is bad and tight, it may take one day or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	Of arm fractures:
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile," and one is small, being the bone that follows the wrist.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other one is large, which is below towards the little finger.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Should the large "foscile" bone break alone or just the small one, or perhaps they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing occurs quickly.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large bones break, healing is more difficult, and the injury is graver than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken, you should slightly extend it and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	If it's a large bone, you must extract it with greater force.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	Place them on a cushion and hold the wrist of their hand higher than the others, with their little finger lower than the other fingers. Have the patient cross themselves over, and place a cushion in front of them higher than they are to prevent any strain or discomfort.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then have your assistants extend their arms to the part below their hands or wrists, while another assistant is above them.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place them in an even position according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it has broken into pieces, place each one back in its position; and if there is a piece missing that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breaking of the wound, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration, warm abscesses appear, so apply I cloth bandages made of rose oil and white wax, that are neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind the cloth bandages gently above, so that the warm abscesses are eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and apply the plaster of the mill powder with abundance of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint for the fracture be closest to and slightly wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And know that there must be six stars on the arm, in several positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	Whether the bone is broken in one place or two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	Hold tightly above the break, more so than elsewhere, and ease off as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the cloths that are placed on the break be soft and moist, not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the thread that is used to hold it be of flax, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And support the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident befalls the limb, such as itching which comes to the limb, then you must sprinkle the limb with warm water until that itch is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the limb rest without constriction.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, or something similar occurs, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you suspect that nourishment cannot reach the limb due to its restriction, it is necessary to soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days until circulation returns, then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, do not release him until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	For that which is around it, then bind his hands to his neck, and keep the necks equal, and guard against movement and turning, and let him sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is healed in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps even twenty days, according to the combinations and complexities of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	On the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that the back of the hand and the knuckles rarely experience breaks but rather frequent dislocations.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the heel of the hand is fractured or bent, it is necessary for the patient to know how to cross their legs, and sit upright directly in front of them evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place their hand on the stretched cloth, and have the assistants stretch out the broken bones, aligning them with the marks, until they are properly joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	et put the plaster and the swabs, if no abscesses come, then place a stent according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is around the edge of the sole, make a sphere out of linen cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their broken foot.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	then strap it with a long cloth and the stent should be made of soft heartwood as large as the sole of your hand; secure it tightly, as is needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, it must be that you place a splint above and another below the broken bone so that the hand remains open and straight, then bind the whole thing around the hand, and tighten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the break is at either of the thumbs then it must be immobilized as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and hold it with a flat surface, and if you see that there is a small straight stick to raise the broken bone, and do not move it;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in another place, like in the index finger or any of the others, make it equal, and bind it with the healthy finger that comes after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together in an 'I' shape, which is better if they move, or place a stick under it, as with the thumb.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and aid those who suffer from them, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often fractured, and it is easily seen when the leg turns forward or backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And restoration is done by binding the ligament above the break, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face; then each minister extends their binding to their respective side equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the hip joint, let one of the ligatures be towards the armpit and the other ligature below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, then let the binding be above the knee, and the extension below.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then the surgeon must align the bone with their two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bind it, if no abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if an abscess does appear, let it cool down, then return to your work and care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The leash is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You must wrap over the fracture with strong bandages doubled in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and thread a long piece of string between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the ends of the string up above.
